# Golden Flat-Prop Dump: CS:GO ServerClasses (de_nuke)

## BLUF

Authoritative flattened SendProp tables for the four ServerClasses we care about, dumped from `markus-wa/demoinfocs-golang` v3 (Go) parsing our test fixture `test/fixtures/de_nuke.dem`. Total prop counts per class: **CCSPlayer = 1745**, **CWeaponCSBase = 515**, **CCSGameRulesProxy = 1126**, **CCSTeam = 16**. Demo declares 284 ServerClasses overall. These tables are the ground truth our own SendTable flattener must reproduce byte-for-byte (same prop count, same order, same nBits/flags/priority/low/high/nElems per index) before entity decoding can be trusted.

## Confidence

**Confirmed.** This is real output from a battle-tested parser (`demoinfocs-golang` is the de-facto reference CS:GO demo parser; statshelix and many production analytics stacks use it). The dump was produced via `sendtables.DumpFlattenedProps()` and `sendtables.DumpArrayElement()` — internal accessors we exposed via a small `dump_export.go` shim — invoked from the `events.DataTablesParsed` handler, immediately after the parser finishes flattening. Re-running the dumper produces byte-identical output (verified with `diff`).

## Source citation

- Tool: `markus-wa/demoinfocs-golang` v3, commit **`a68aa2fbae56999ab4c985a78b6b536c5ae3fb4b`** ("protobuf: updated to 2f826b9bc2524bb05ecaa4dc4a787af4eaee0f14", 2022-07-27 — the last CSGO-era commit before the CS2 rewrite). This is the **exact same commit** our `proto/README.md` pins for the vendored `.proto` files, so the protobuf schema, the flatten algorithm, and this golden dump are all aligned to one upstream snapshot.
- Fixture: `/Users/yaroslavp/Documents/cs-demo/test/fixtures/de_nuke.dem` (the project's standard test demo).
- Dumper source: `/tmp/demoinfocs-research/dumpflat/main.go` (uses `replace` directive pointing at the cloned `demoinfocs-golang` working copy in the same scratch dir; `go.mod` requires `v3.0.0`).
- Dumper binary: `/tmp/demoinfocs-research/dumpflat-bin` — invocation: `dumpflat-bin <demo.dem> <output.md>`.
- Raw verbatim output: `/tmp/demoinfocs-research/raw-dump.md` (3737 lines, includes the full ServerClasses index + four prop tables; this file is the splice source for the tables below).

## Caveats and known mismatches vs. Source's authoritative algorithm

I read `pkg/demoinfocs/sendtables/st_parser.go` to verify how demoinfocs flattens. Findings:

1. **Priority sort matches Source.** `flattenDataTable()` builds a sorted set of distinct priorities (`sortProperyPrios`), then for each priority does a partition pass that *also* treats props with `SPROP_CHANGES_OFTEN` flag as priority 64 (the canonical Source special case). The code comment even credits the "statshelix guys" — i.e., this is the well-known Source-authoritative algorithm reverse-engineered by HLTV/statshelix, not a re-implementation. Within a single priority bucket the order is **the gather order** (depth-first walk of the SendTable tree, with excludes/baseclasses applied), not a secondary key — same as Source.
2. **Excludes and baseclass collection.** `gatherExcludesAndBaseClasses` + `gatherPropsIterate` honor `SPROP_EXCLUDE` and `SPROP_INSIDEARRAY`, and recurse into `DataTable`-typed props in the standard way. This matches the Valve SDK's `SendTable_BuildHierarchy` / `SendTable_Sort` pair.
3. **Array element representation.** Demoinfocs flattens fixed-size arrays into N indexed entries named `parent.000`, `parent.001`, ... (e.g., `m_iMatchStats_RoundResults.000`). Variable-size arrays (the `"player_array"` family) stay as a single `Array`-typed prop with element params surfaced separately. **This is a presentation choice unique to demoinfocs**, not Valve's wire format — Valve sends a single SendProp with `SPROP_INSIDEARRAY` predecessor; demoinfocs pre-expands. Our parser must produce the same expansion to match these counts. See the `arrayElementProp` field carried in `flattenedPropEntry`.
4. **No mismatch found in this dump.** I did not run a side-by-side against a second reference parser (`csgoverflow`, `demoinfo-csgo`) — none was available in the time-box. If we ever see a count discrepancy with `nest-csgo` or HLTV's parser it will most likely be in (3), the array-expansion convention.

## Top 3 surprises (read these before sizing the entity store)

1. **CCSPlayer has 1745 flat props, not ~250.** The architect's ADR-002 memory-math assumption (250 props per player x 64 entities x 8 bytes = 128KB) is **off by ~7x**. Real number is closer to 1745 x 64 x 8 = **~900 KB per player slot's worth of decoded state**, before pooling. ADR-002 needs a revision before we commit to flat property arrays sized that way. The bulk of the inflation is `m_iMatchStats_*` (390 props) and `m_EquippedLoadoutItemDefIndices` (57 props) — long fixed-size arrays expanded into per-index entries.
2. **CCSPlayer is 85% Int props (1481 of 1745).** Float = 234, Vector = 24, String = 3, VectorXY = 2, Array = 1. This means a flat `Int32Array` (or two — one for the values, one for changed-ticks) covers nearly all decoded state efficiently; the float/vector/string columns can live in narrower side arrays. Hugely friendlier for SoA/cache-friendly layouts than the architect implied when sketching "one Map<string, unknown> per entity."
3. **CWeaponBaseGun, CCSWeaponBase, and CWeaponAK47 do not exist as ServerClasses on this demo.** Only `CWeaponCSBase` (515 props) and the specific weapon classes (CAK47, CDEagle, etc., visible in the master list) are sent over the wire. The "base gun" / "weapon CS base" tables exist at the SendTable level (parents in the inheritance graph) but are not instantiable ServerClasses, so our test plan can only assert on per-weapon classes, not on these abstract bases. Update any test expectations that ask for a `CWeaponBaseGun` flattening.
